# Wave 3 — Motif Studio — adjudicated decisions

> 69 items · 67 DECIDED · 2 not-a-question · 0 deferred · 0 escalated.

> **These are INSTRUCTIONS, not suggestions.** Each was settled by reading source. Do not re-open a
> decided question. Where this contradicts the wave plan, **this file wins.**

## Decisions

### Q-33-BEM1-REPO-COLLAPSE
MUST-BUILD — collapse the four predicates to one, exactly as BE-M1(b)(c)(d)(e) states. Code confirms all four sites verbatim; nothing contradicts §0. Build it as follows.

(b) ADD to services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:
    async def current_for_nodes(self, project_id: UUID, node_ids: list[UUID]) -> dict[UUID, MotifApplication]
    SQL: SELECT DISTINCT ON (outline_node_id) {_SELECT_COLS} FROM motif_application
         WHERE project_id = $1 AND outline_node_id = ANY($2)
         ORDER BY outline_node_id, created_at DESC
    Build the dict via the existing _row() helper (NOT model_validate + _jsonb_loads — that is the router's private path), keyed on app.outline_node_id, skipping None. Empty node_ids -> {}. Keep the project_id filter (kinds-bug tenancy rule).

(d) RENAME by_nodes -> history_by_nodes (same body, list, ORDER BY created_at ASC). Update its docstring: it is the multi-node HISTORY read, not "the bound motif per node". Sole caller stays engine/arc_apply.py:590.

DELETE ConformanceTraceReader.apps_by_nodes (routers/conformance.py:95-113) entirely and repoint conformance.py:412 to MotifApplicationRepo(self._pool or get_pool()).current_for_nodes(project_id, node_ids). SAFE: the router-private SELECT omits structure_node_id while the repo's _SELECT_COLS includes it, so the repo returns a strict superset of the columns MotifApplication needs. Leave latest_completed_by_nodes (conformance.py:191) alone — different table.

REPOINT plan.py:1034-1036: replace `bound = await apps.by_nodes(project_id, [node_id]); app = bound[0] if bound else None` with `app = (await apps.current_for_nodes(project_id, [node_id])).get(node_id)`. Downstream None-guard is unchanged.

REPOINT plan.py:1193-1197: replace the by_nodes call + the hand-rolled `apps_by_node = {a.outline_node_id: a for a in apps ...}` dict-collapse (and its now-false "by_nodes is created_at ASC -> last wins" comment) with a single `apps_by_node = await MotifApplicationRepo(get_pool()).current_for_nodes(project_id, [s.id for s in scenes])`. `bound_ids` below it keeps working unchanged (it already iterates apps_by_node.values()).

(c) _MOTIF_CHIPS_SQL (plan_overlay.py:112-123) — belt-and-braces. IMPORTANT: DISTINCT ON cannot be added inline; Postgres requires ORDER BY to lead with the DISTINCT ON expression, which would destroy the existing `ORDER BY ma.created_at, ma.id` the chip renderer depends on. Wrap it:
    SELECT * FROM (
      SELECT DISTINCT ON (COALESCE(ma.outline_node_id, ma.structure_node_id))
             COALESCE(ma.outline_node_id, ma.structure_node_id) AS node_ref,
             ma.motif_id, ma.motif_version AS pinned_version,
             m.name AS title, m.version AS live_version,
             ma.created_at, ma.id
      FROM motif_application ma JOIN motif m ON m.id = ma.motif_id
      WHERE ma.book_id = $1
        AND (ma.outline_node_id IS NOT NULL OR ma.structure_node_id IS NOT NULL)
      ORDER BY COALESCE(ma.outline_node_id, ma.structure_node_id), ma.created_at DESC
    ) t ORDER BY t.created_at, t.id
Changes nothing visible today (M-BUG-3 is REFUTED) — hardening only.

(e) set_role_binding (motif_application.py:137-163) — add a required `application_id: UUID` param and `AND id = $5` to the UPDATE's WHERE (KEEP project_id + outline_node_id in the WHERE — they are the tenancy filter, not redundant). plan.py:1051 already holds the app from the (b) repoint, so pass `app.id`.

TESTS (update, do not add regressions for M-BUG-2/M-BUG-3):
  - tests/integration/db/test_conformance_trace.py:110,139,190 — apps_by_nodes -> current_for_nodes (assertions unchanged; the project-scoped-not-actor-scoped test must survive the move).
  - tests/integration/db/test_rnode_p1_dataplane.py:124 — same repoint.
  - tests/integration/db/test_arc_apply_roundtrip.py:201 — by_nodes -> history_by_nodes.
  - tests/unit/test_scene_motif_rebind_chain.py:51-57 — the FakeRepo must grow current_for_nodes (returning a dict) and set_role_binding must take application_id.
  - NEW: an integration test asserting a scene re-bound twice yields exactly ONE row from current_for_nodes and that it is the NEWEST (assert on created_at / motif_id).

EXPECTATION TO SET FOR REVIEW: no test here can red on the old code. All four readers are correct today — the invariant holds by convention across the 5 writers (spec §1.1). This is a readability + robustness collapse, and the enforcement is BE-M1(a)'s partial UNIQUE index, which MUST land in the same commit (with its back-fill probe output pasted in VERIFY). Do not re-raise M-BUG-2 or M-BUG-3 — both REFUTED.

*Evidence:* services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:94-111 (by_nodes -> list, ORDER BY created_at ASC, docstring "The bound motif per node" = singular language over a plural return) and :137-163 (set_role_binding UPDATE ... WHERE project_id=$1 AND outline_node_id=$2, no id filter) and :28-31 (_SELECT_COLS includes structure_node_id); services/composition-service/app/routers/conformance.py:95-113 (router-private ConformanceTraceReader.apps_by_nodes -> dict, DISTINCT ON (outline_node_id) ORDER BY outline_node_id, created_at DESC — a duplicate of the repo query whose SELECT list OMITS structure_node_id) called at :412; services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:1034-1036 (bound = await apps.by_nodes(...); app = bound[0]) vs :1193-1197 (same repo call, hand-rolled dict-collapse, comment "by_nodes is created_at ASC -> last wins on a re-bind" — the file contradicts itself); services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/plan_overlay.py:112-123 (_MOTIF_CHIPS_SQL, no DISTINCT ON, ORDER BY ma.created_at, ma.id); services/composition-service/app/engine/arc_apply.py:590 (the one genuine multi-node history read to preserve). Spec row: docs/specs/2026-07-01-writing-studio/30_TOOL_GUI_GAP_AUDIT_AND_PLAN.md:440 (BE-M1) + :66-68 (M-BUG-1 CONFIRMED; M-BUG-2/M-BUG-3 REFUTED).

### Q-33-BEM1-DDL
BUILD IT — the code confirms the invariant holds today, so the partial UNIQUE index is safe and is the fix. Exact instructions (Size S, one service, no cross-service seam):

(1) DDL — `services/composition-service/app/db/migrate.py`.
  a. In the base motif_application block, REPLACE line 882 (`CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_motif_application_node ON motif_application(outline_node_id);`) with:
     `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS uq_motif_application_node ON motif_application(outline_node_id) WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL;`
     (Keep `idx_motif_application_book_motif` (881) and `idx_motif_application_project` (883) as-is.)
  b. In the additive-migration tail, next to the existing `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_motif_application_structure` (migrate.py:1250), add `DROP INDEX IF EXISTS idx_motif_application_node;` so already-migrated DBs shed the now-redundant ordinary index (the partial UNIQUE fully serves every `outline_node_id = ANY(...)` lookup — `by_nodes`/`apps_by_nodes`/`set_role_binding`/`delete_for_nodes` never probe NULL). Do NOT re-order: `migrate.py` is one idempotent re-runnable script, so both fresh and migrated DBs converge.
  c. Do NOT wrap the index creation in a dedup/DELETE block. Per spec 33 §BE-M1(a), if the probe below returns rows the invariant is refuted and the plan must be re-opened — a silent auto-dedup would destroy binding-ledger rows (a destructive action; the run policy says STOP for those).

(2) Back-fill probe (mandatory VERIFY evidence, paste the literal output):
  `SELECT outline_node_id, count(*) FROM motif_application WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL GROUP BY 1 HAVING count(*) > 1;`
  Expected: 0 rows. Grounding for that expectation (I traced all 5 writers — this is the code proof the spec's §1.1 "convention" rests on):
    - arc_apply.py:438 `delete_for_nodes` → :485 `insert_many` (delete-then-insert)
    - motif_select.py:470 delete (archived scenes) → :491 insert onto FRESH node ids; :526 delete on undo
    - plan.py:843 delete → :844 insert (single-node re-bind)
    - plan.py:774 and plan.py:1377 insert onto FRESH scene ids created in the same request, guarded by `created["replay"]`
  Every path is delete-then-insert or insert-onto-a-new-node-id ⇒ no node can hold 2 live rows.

(3) Writer hardening the spec didn't cover, and MUST land with the index (otherwise the index converts a latent bug into a live 500 AFTER the tree is committed): `plan.py:776-780` and `plan.py:1378-1381` currently catch ONLY `asyncpg.ForeignKeyViolationError` and soft-skip the advisory ledger. Widen both to `except (asyncpg.ForeignKeyViolationError, asyncpg.UniqueViolationError)` with the same `logger.warning(... ledger skipped)` — the ledger is advisory, the tree commit must not fail on it. Do NOT add `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` to `insert_many` (repositories/motif_application.py:66-82): every real writer deletes first, and a silent upsert would mask a future append-instead-of-replace regression — which is exactly what this index exists to catch.

(4) Test — add to `services/composition-service/tests/integration/db/test_motif_migrate.py` (real-PG, throwaway DB, already the home of the 4.5 motif_application scope-guard test): "4.9 — one live binding per scene node": after `run_migrations`, insert a motif_application for node N; a SECOND insert with the same `outline_node_id` raises `asyncpg.UniqueViolationError`; a delete-then-insert (the re-bind shape) succeeds; and TWO rows with `outline_node_id IS NULL` and distinct `structure_node_id` both insert (the partial exemption). Re-run `run_migrations` twice to prove the new index is idempotent (mirrors 4.1).

(5) BE-M1(b)-(e) (the reader collapse: `current_for_nodes`, delete `ConformanceTraceReader.apps_by_nodes`, repoint plan.py:1035 / plan.py:1193, DISTINCT ON in `_MOTIF_CHIPS_SQL`, rename `by_nodes`→`history_by_nodes`) stay as spec'd and land in the SAME slice — (a) alone leaves the four-shaped readers in place. Do NOT budget regression tests for M-BUG-2/M-BUG-3 (REFUTED).

Default I am picking (veto-able): dropping `idx_motif_application_node` in step (1b). If the PO would rather keep the redundant index, delete step (1b) — nothing else changes.

`/review-impl` runs at the completion of the wave; any bug it finds is fixed before the wave closes.

*Evidence:* services/composition-service/app/db/migrate.py:882 — `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_motif_application_node ON motif_application(outline_node_id);` (ordinary, non-unique; the table DDL is at :869-883, the H-5 scope-guard trigger at :887-905, the additive `structure_node_id` column + index at :1247-1250). The 5 writers that hold the invariant by convention: services/composition-service/app/engine/arc_apply.py:438+485, app/engine/motif_select.py:470+491 and :526, app/routers/plan.py:774, :843-844, :1377. The FK-only except clauses that would 500 under the new index: app/routers/plan.py:776-780 and :1378-1381. Repo: app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:48-92 (`insert_many`, no ON CONFLICT), :165-186 (`delete_for_nodes`).

### Q-33-BEM3-MOTIF-LINK-REST
MUST-BUILD as REST, exactly as the spec states — the repo methods exist, the routes do not, and per CLAUDE.md "missing infrastructure is unbuilt work, not a blocker". Build it in the EXISTING `services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py` (prefix `/v1/composition`, already mounted at `app/main.py:226`). Do NOT create a `MotifLinkRepo` or a new router module.

THREE ROUTES (~40 lines), each a thin wrapper on `MotifRepo` via the existing `get_motif_repo` dep:

1) `GET /motifs/{motif_id}/links` — query: `direction: str = "both"` (validate in {out,in,both} → 400 otherwise, mirroring `server.py:2627`), `kinds: list[str] | None = Query(None)`, `limit: int = 200`, `book_id: UUID | None = None`. If `book_id` is given → `await _gate_book(grant, book_id, caller, GrantLevel.VIEW)` FIRST (motif.py:56). Then `repo.list_links(caller, motif_id, direction=..., kinds=..., limit=..., book_id=...)` → `200 {"motif_id":…, "links":[…], "count": n}`.
   ⚠ CORRECTION to the spec's "404 uniform H13" for THIS route: an invisible anchor returns `[]` from the repo and MUST be served as `200` with an empty list — NOT 404. That is the shipped MCP behavior (`server.py:2635-2637`: "empty is indistinguishable from 'no edges', no existence oracle") and it is the IDOR-safe choice. The `motif_repo.py:225` docstring claiming "router maps the empty/None to H13" is stale drift — follow the code. H13 (`_NOT_FOUND`, motif.py:69) applies to the WRITE routes only.

2) `POST /motifs/{motif_id}/links` → `status_code=201`. Body (a `_ForbidExtra` pydantic model, house style): `to_motif_id: UUID`, `kind: str = Field(pattern="^(composed_of|precedes|variant_of)$")`, `ord: int | None = None` (include it — `create_link` and the MCP arg model both take it, and `ord` is what orders a `precedes` chain in `list_links`), `book_id: UUID | None = None`. `from_motif_id` comes from the PATH. If `book_id` → `_gate_book(..., GrantLevel.EDIT)` first (never VIEW — matches `server.py:2665-2668`). Then `repo.create_link(...)` inside try/except, mapping:
   • `LookupError` → `HTTPException(404, detail=_NOT_FOUND)`  (endpoint not owned / not in this book's shared tier)
   • `asyncpg.UniqueViolationError` → `HTTPException(409, detail={"code":"MOTIF_LINK_EXISTS","message":"that edge already exists"})`
   • `asyncpg.CheckViolationError` → `HTTPException(409, …)` — **this is the case the spec is protecting; un-handled it is a 500.** RELAY THE REASON BY CLASSIFYING IT, do not pass `str(e)` through: if `getattr(e, "constraint_name", None) == "motif_link_distinct"` → code `MOTIF_LINK_SELF`; elif `"cycle" in str(e)` → `MOTIF_LINK_CYCLE`; else → `MOTIF_LINK_CROSS_TIER`. Reason for classifying rather than echoing: the trigger's cross-tier RAISE interpolates raw owner_user_id/book_id of BOTH endpoints (`migrate.py:834`) — echoing it verbatim is a leak-shaped habit even though the repo's app-gate makes both endpoints caller-scoped by then.
   201 body = `link.model_dump(mode="json")`.

3) `DELETE /motif-links/{link_id}` → `status_code=204`, query `book_id: UUID | None = None`. If `book_id` → `_gate_book(..., GrantLevel.EDIT)`. `deleted = await repo.delete_link(caller, link_id, book_id=...)`; `if not deleted: raise HTTPException(404, detail=_NOT_FOUND)`; else `return Response(status_code=204)`. Keep the spec's non-nested path (link ids are global) — it does not collide with the existing `/motifs/{motif_id}` routes.

TESTS — add to the EXISTING `services/composition-service/tests/unit/test_motif_router.py` (house style already there: `app.dependency_overrides` + `StubMotifRepo` + a stub grant, see its lines 133-156; extend `StubMotifRepo` with `list_links`/`create_link`/`delete_link`). Required cases, one assert each: (a) GET direction=out/in/both passes through; (b) GET with a bogus `direction` → 400; (c) GET on an invisible anchor (stub returns `[]`) → **200 + `count==0`**, asserting NOT 404; (d) POST happy → 201; (e) POST where the stub raises `asyncpg.UniqueViolationError` → 409 `MOTIF_LINK_EXISTS`; (f) POST where the stub raises `asyncpg.CheckViolationError("motif_link cycle on precedes via …")` → **409 `MOTIF_LINK_CYCLE`, explicitly asserting `!= 500`** (this is the spec's stated failure mode); (g) POST where the stub raises `LookupError` → 404 `MOTIF_NOT_FOUND`; (h) POST/DELETE with `book_id` and an insufficient grant → 403, and with no grant → 404 (the `_gate_book` contract); (i) DELETE deleted=True → 204, deleted=False → 404. Repo-level SQL semantics are already covered by `tests/integration/db/test_motif_repo.py` — do not duplicate them.

NOT via the FE bridge — confirmed correct: `tools.controller.ts:20-23` says nothing there writes or deletes, and this is a POST + DELETE. Consistent with sealed §0 (no PO-1..4 decision touches this).

*Evidence:* services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_repo.py:215 (list_links) / :275 (create_link) / :320 (delete_link) — exist; no MotifLinkRepo anywhere. services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py — 454 lines, prefix /v1/composition, mounted app/main.py:226; `grep "link" app/routers/motif.py` → ZERO hits, so the graph has no REST surface today (GG-1 violation: agent-only). Reference impl to mirror = the 3 MCP tools at app/mcp/server.py:2599 / :2644 / :2691, incl. the VIEW-vs-EDIT gate split (:2665) and the no-existence-oracle empty list (:2635). The 409 source: app/db/migrate.py:805-861 `motif_link_guard()` RAISEs USING ERRCODE='check_violation' for cross-tier (:834, interpolates raw owner/book UUIDs) and cycle (:849), plus the `motif_link_distinct` table CHECK (:795) for self-links — all three arrive as asyncpg.CheckViolationError and are a 500 unless caught. Existing helpers to reuse: _gate_book (motif.py:56 → OwnershipError=404 / InsufficientGrant=403), _NOT_FOUND (motif.py:69, the H13 constant), and the 409-detail-dict shape at motif.py:126/140/278. Test harness: tests/unit/test_motif_router.py:133-156.

### Q-33-BEM5-DELETED
CLAIM VERIFIED — BE-M5 STAYS DELETED. Do NOT build any arc-suggest route in spec 33 / Wave 3.

Builder instructions (three concrete rules):

1. WAVE 3 (spec 33) ships MOTIF suggest ONLY — BE-M4: `GET /v1/composition/works/{project_id}/motifs/suggest?chapter_id=&limit=10&detail=summary|full`, added to `services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py` (router prefix `/v1/composition`, declared at motif.py:53). Reuse the body of the `composition_motif_suggest_for_chapter` MCP handler. Wave 3 adds NO arc route, NO "Suggest an arc" button, and does NOT touch `tools.controller.ts`.

2. ARC suggest is Wave 4 / spec 34 §5 BE-7b, and its ONE contract is `POST /v1/composition/arc-templates/suggest` with body `{project_id, premise?, genre?, limit=5, detail='summary'|'full'}` → `{candidates:[{arc_template, score, match_reason}], ...meta}`, 404 uniform H13 on VIEW-deny. Build it in `services/composition-service/app/routers/arc.py` (the file already owns every other `/arc-templates/*` route: :106/:132/:157/:172/:193/:233/:249/:278). It is a thin wrapper: `MotifRetriever.retrieve_arcs(tc.user_id, book_id=meta.book_id, project_id=pid, premise=..., genre=..., limit=...)` then `apply_response_contract(..., ref_fields=_ARC_REF_FIELDS, detail=detail)` — i.e. copy `server.py:2299-2325` verbatim. Keep `limit=5` and keep `detail` (Context Budget Law §6b). No path collision: `/arc-templates/suggest` is one segment and no `POST /arc-templates/{arc_id}` exists.

3. The "Suggest an arc ✨" button's landing site is `arc-inspector` / `arc-templates` in Wave 4 — NOT `motif-library`. If a Wave-3 builder finds themselves writing `GET /books/{book_id}/arcs/suggest`, or adding `composition_arc_suggest` to `FE_BRIDGE_TOOL_ALLOWLIST`, they have taken a wrong turn: the tool has no `book_id` arg (server.py:2288) and the allowlist's own contract bars it (a free read has no reason to take the paid agentic path, and it would make the wave cross-service).

Default I am picking (veto-able): the wrong `GET /books/{bid}/arcs/suggest` shape is dead — it is not "also built for convenience". One tool, one REST mirror, POST-shaped to match the tool's arg set.

*Evidence:* services/composition-service/app/mcp/server.py:2287-2298 — `async def composition_arc_suggest(ctx, project_id: str, premise=None, genre=None, limit: int = 5, detail: Literal['summary','full'] = 'full')`; book resolved at :2303 via `_book_or_deny(works, tc, pid, GrantLevel.VIEW)` — NO `book_id` arg, default limit=5 (not 10), so spec 33's `GET /books/{book_id}/arcs/suggest?limit=10` was a wrong contract. Engine: services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_retrieve.py:279-284 `retrieve_arcs(caller_id, *, book_id, project_id, premise, genre, limit=5)`. Route inventory: services/composition-service/app/routers/arc.py:63 (prefix /v1/composition) owns /arc-templates/* at :106,:132,:157,:172,:193,:233,:249,:278 — no suggest route exists; services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py:151-386 — no suggest route either. Owner-of-record: docs/specs/2026-07-01-writing-studio/34_arc_templates_and_deconstruct.md:206 (BE-7b) and docs/specs/2026-07-01-writing-studio/30_TOOL_GUI_GAP_AUDIT_AND_PLAN.md:299-300 (BE-6 de-duped to motif-only; BE-7 is the ONE arc-suggest owner). No conflict with plan 30 §0 PO-1..PO-4.

### Q-33-BEM2-CAP-N
N = 600 chars, PER-BINDING — plus a hard PER-BLOCK ceiling of 2000 chars. Both, not either/or: the ≤3-binding count cap does not bound the block (one motif's preconditions/effects/info_asymmetry are unbounded author text), and the per-binding cap alone still admits 3×600 + header growth, so the block cap is the load-bearing one that actually closes the Context-Budget-Law hole. Concretely, for BE-M2 in services/composition-service/app/packer/lenses.py + pack.py + config.py:

1) SIGNATURE — mirror gather_arc's cap plumbing exactly (lenses.py:260):
   async def gather_motifs(motif_app_repo, motif_repo, *, project_id, node, chapter_id,
                           bindings_cap: int = 3, binding_chars_cap: int = 600,
                           block_chars_cap: int = 2000) -> str

2) CONFIG — add three settings in services/composition-service/app/config.py immediately after
   `pack_open_promises_cap: int = 8` (config.py:109), with the same comment intent ("bounded so a
   large ledger can't crowd out canon/beat"):
       pack_motifs_cap: int = 3
       pack_motif_binding_chars_cap: int = 600
       pack_motifs_block_chars_cap: int = 2000
   Rationale to put in the comment: the <motifs> block rides OUTSIDE enforce_budget (pack.py:522),
   so these caps are the ONLY thing bounding it.

3) WHERE THE NUMBERS COME FROM (do not re-litigate):
   - 3 bindings = the spec's own stated cap, and the same "count cap" discipline as
     pack_open_promises_cap=8 (lenses.py:356 `promises[:open_promises_cap]`).
   - 2000 chars/block = GUIDE_MAX_LEN (sanitize.py:31), the packer's ONLY existing char ceiling and
     the one other author-authored free-text surface. Reuse it rather than inventing a number.
   - 600 chars/binding = 2000/3 rounded down to a round number, so 3 full-size bindings (1800) fit
     under the block ceiling with headroom for the "Motifs:" header lines. ~500-650 tokens worst
     case against a default pack_token_budget of 6000 (config.py:50) — ≈10%, in the same weight class
     as the capped arc frame.

4) HOW TO APPLY (order matters):
   a. Resolve scene → chapter → arc binding chain (mirror gather_arc). Take at most `bindings_cap`
      applications, deterministically ordered (most-specific scope first, then created_at DESC —
      reuse MotifApplicationRepo.current_for_nodes from BE-M1).
   b. Render ONE binding into its text, sanitize_lore() every author string FIRST (SEC3), THEN
      truncate that rendered per-binding string to `binding_chars_cap`. Truncate AFTER sanitize, never
      before — truncating first can chop a fullwidth-escape mid-sequence.
   c. Mark the truncation, never silently: append " …[truncated]" when a cut happened (Context Budget
      Law §6a cross-cutting: "any reject/overflow/drop returns an actionable notice, never a silent
      truncation").
   d. Join the ≤3 binding strings, then apply the final belt-and-braces block clamp:
      text = text[:block_chars_cap] (with the same "…[truncated]" marker). This is the guarantee that
      survives any future field being added to the render.
   e. Keep gather_arc's best-effort posture: any repo failure → return "" (the frame THINS, never
      fails a pack).

5) WIRING — pass the settings at the pack.py call site the same way arc_gated passes
   settings.pack_open_promises_cap (pack.py:332-337), and emit the block beside <arc> at pack.py:522.

6) DO NOT do either of these (both are scope creep and both break existing arc tests):
   - Do NOT move <motifs> (or <arc>) inside enforce_budget. pack.py:515-521 documents the
     outside-budget posture deliberately; the char cap is what makes it safe.
   - Do NOT change how token_count accounts for <arc> (pack.py:536 already excludes it). That
     understatement is pre-existing and is not BE-M2's to fix.

7) TEST (add to the BE-M2 real-DB effect test file test_pack_motifs_wired.py, which is already the
   wave's hard gate): (i) seed a motif whose `preconditions` is a 10,000-char string → assert the
   rendered <motifs> block is ≤ 2000 chars and contains the truncation marker; (ii) seed 5 resolvable
   bindings → assert exactly 3 render; (iii) assert a crafted motif name containing "</motifs>" is
   fullwidth-escaped (sanitize_lore ran before truncation).

DEFAULT NOTED FOR PO VETO: 600/2000 is a defensible default derived from the packer's own existing
ceilings, not a measured optimum. If the PO wants the motif frame to weigh more or less against the
6000-token pack budget, they change the two config values — no code change.

*Evidence:* services/composition-service/app/packer/lenses.py:260 (`open_promises_cap: int = 8` — gather_arc's ONLY cap is a COUNT cap, applied at lenses.py:356 `promises[:open_promises_cap]`; there is no char cap to inherit) · services/composition-service/app/config.py:109 (`pack_open_promises_cap: int = 8`, comment: "protected in the budget but bounded so a large ledger can't crowd out canon/beat" — the settings-fed-cap pattern to mirror) · services/composition-service/app/packer/sanitize.py:31 (`GUIDE_MAX_LEN = 2000` — the packer's ONLY existing char ceiling, on the one other author-authored free-text surface; this is where 2000 comes from) · services/composition-service/app/packer/pack.py:511 + 522-524 (`bres = B.enforce_budget(...)` THEN `prompt = f"<arc>\n{arc_text}\n</arc>" + ...` — the arc block is appended AFTER budget enforcement, and pack.py:536 `token_count=bres.total_tokens` excludes it: this is the exact hole an uncapped <motifs> block would widen) · services/composition-service/app/config.py:50 (`pack_token_budget: int = 6000` — the budget the 2000-char cap is ~10% of)

### Q-33-BEM3-GRANT-CHECK
DERIVE the scope from the loaded row; DROP `book_id` from BE-M3's REST surface entirely (no `?book_id=` on DELETE, no `book_id` in the POST body). The client never supplies the scope key. Build it in three parts:

(1) ROOT-CAUSE FIX IN THE REPO (do this first — it closes a live grant-bypass that exists TODAY on the MCP path too, so it is fix-now per CLAUDE.md, not a defer). The no-`book_id` path currently gates on ownership only, but a `book_shared` motif still carries its adopter's `owner_user_id`, and the DB trigger's shared arm (migrate.py:827-831) admits shared<->shared same-book edges regardless of owner. Net: omitting `book_id` lets a caller create/delete edges in a book's SHARED graph with ZERO grant check (survives grant revocation). Fix: confine the default path to the private tier.
  - `motif_repo.py:304-309` (create_link, default arm): also SELECT `book_shared`; reject unless BOTH endpoints are `owner_user_id == caller_id AND NOT book_shared` -> raise LookupError("both endpoints must be private motifs you own").
  - `motif_repo.py:341-344` (delete_link, default arm): add `AND NOT m.book_shared` to the WHERE.
  A shared edge is then reachable ONLY through the book_id path, which is EDIT-gated. This fixes REST and MCP at one seam.

(2) NEW REPO HELPER — `MotifRepo.link_scope(link_id) -> {"from_motif_id","owner_user_id","book_shared","book_id"} | None`:
  `SELECT l.from_motif_id, m.owner_user_id, m.book_shared, m.book_id FROM motif_link l JOIN motif m ON m.id = l.from_motif_id WHERE l.id = $1`
  Also `MotifRepo.tiers_of([motif_id,...]) -> {id: (owner_user_id, book_shared, book_id)}` (create_link already runs this SELECT internally; expose it).

(3) THE ROUTES in `services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py` (prefix `/v1/composition`, router.py:53), each DERIVING the gate from the loaded row and reusing `_gate_book` (motif.py:56-65 — none->404, under-tier->403):
  - `GET /motifs/{motif_id}/links?direction=out|in|both` — load the anchor's tier via `tiers_of([motif_id])`. If missing -> 404 `_NOT_FOUND`. If `book_shared` -> `_gate_book(grant, row.book_id, user, GrantLevel.VIEW)` then `repo.list_links(user, motif_id, direction=..., book_id=row.book_id)`. Else -> `repo.list_links(user, motif_id, direction=...)` (no book_id). Empty list on an invisible anchor stays 200 `{links:[]}` (IDOR-safe, H13).
  - `POST /motifs/{motif_id}/links` body `{to_motif_id, kind}` — load BOTH endpoints via `tiers_of`. If either missing -> 404. If BOTH `book_shared` AND same `book_id` -> `_gate_book(..., GrantLevel.EDIT)` on THAT derived book_id, then `create_link(..., book_id=derived)`. If NEITHER is `book_shared` -> the private path `create_link(...)` (repo enforces both-owned). Mixed tiers -> 404 `_NOT_FOUND` (the trigger would reject it anyway; do not leak which endpoint). -> 201 `{link}`. Map `asyncpg.UniqueViolationError` -> 409 "that edge already exists"; `asyncpg.CheckViolationError` -> 409 relaying the trigger's reason ("self-link, cycle, or cross-tier") — do NOT flatten to 500 (spec 33 §3a is explicit).
  - `DELETE /motif-links/{link_id}` — NO query param. `scope = repo.link_scope(link_id)`; None -> 404. If `scope.book_shared` -> `_gate_book(grant, scope.book_id, user, GrantLevel.EDIT)` then `delete_link(user, link_id, book_id=scope.book_id)`. Else -> `delete_link(user, link_id)`. Not deleted -> 404. -> 204.

So the 403 fires exactly when the LOADED row is a `book_shared` edge and the caller's grant on THAT row's own book is below EDIT (VIEW for the GET). A caller cannot name a book to widen or dodge the gate, because the book is read off the row.

TESTS (name them in the slice): (a) `create_link` between two OWNED `book_shared` motifs with NO book_id is REFUSED (this test REDS before fix (1) — it is the bypass); (b) `delete_link` with no book_id does NOT delete a shared-tier edge; (c) DELETE /motif-links/{id} on a shared edge with VIEW-only grant -> 403; with no grant -> 404; with EDIT -> 204; (d) POST links mixed-tier -> 404; (e) trigger cycle -> 409 with the reason relayed, not 500.

NOTE FOR THE PO (veto-able default): this drops the `book_id?` field the spec sketched in 33 §4's BE-M3 row. That row's contract is superseded — the param was never load-bearing (it can only ever equal the row's own book), and removing it makes the 403 derivable instead of client-asserted. Spec 33 §4's BE-M3 request column should be edited to match. The MCP tools KEEP their `book_id` arg (agents pass it as a tier hint and it is already EDIT/VIEW-gated) — fix (1) makes that arg's absence safe rather than exploitable. Sibling routes (`PATCH`/`DELETE /motifs/{id}?book_id=`, motif.py:286-380) keep their param and are out of scope here, but they share the shape — if `/review-impl` at wave close wants them derived too, that is a follow-up, not this slice.

*Evidence:* services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_repo.py:308-309 (create_link default arm gates on `owned.get(from) != caller_id or owned.get(to) != caller_id` — ownership ONLY, no `NOT book_shared`); motif_repo.py:343 (`WHERE l.id = $2 AND m.id = l.from_motif_id AND m.owner_user_id = $1` — same gap on delete); services/composition-service/app/db/migrate.py:827-831 (motif_link_guard `same_tier` shared arm: `(from_shared AND to_shared AND from_book = to_book)` — owner-agnostic, so the two above pass the DB trigger => shared-graph write with NO grant check when `book_id` is omitted); services/composition-service/app/mcp/server.py:2634 (`_gate(tc, bid, GrantLevel.VIEW)` on list), :2665 (`_gate(tc, bid, GrantLevel.EDIT)` on create), :2716 (EDIT on delete) — the existing route-side gate BE-M3 must mirror; services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py:56-65 (`_gate_book`: OwnershipError->404 no-oracle, InsufficientGrant->403 — the exact 403 the spec means); motif_repo.py:215 list_links / :275 create_link / :320 delete_link (the three repo methods BE-M3 wraps); motif_repo.py:506 `get_in_book` (the VIEW-gated shared-tier read list_links already delegates to).

(2) `regenerate-to-beat` exists in ZERO backend routes — `grep -rn "regenerate.to.beat|regenerate_to_beat" services/ contracts/` returns only a stale COMMENT, no route def. All 3 references are frontend-only, so every click 404s today.
(3) `POST /works/{project_id}/generate` (engine.py:326, GenerateBody engine.py:91-105) is ALREADY scene-targeted: `outline_node_id: UUID` (required), `model_source: Literal["user_model","platform_model"]` (required), `model_ref: UUID` (required), `operation: str = "draft_scene"`, `mode: Literal["cowrite","auto"] = "cowrite"`.

Its only legitimate successor is the ALREADY-SHIPPED `commitAndGenerate(sceneId)` on the same hook (line 73) which routes to `{tab:'compose', sceneId}` — the ComposePanel generate path. Do not re-add a mutation.

STEP 3 — ⚠ THE SPEC'S DELETE-LIST IS INCOMPLETE — there is a THIRD call site it does not name, and step 1 will red the typecheck on it. `useConformanceTrace.regenerateToBeat` (hooks/useConformanceTrace.ts:25-28) also calls `motifApi.regenerateToBeat`, and it IS wired to a live button: `ConformanceTraceView.tsx:69` passes `onRegenerate={(id) => trace.regenerateToBeat.mutate(id)}` per scene row. using `compositionApi.generateAuto` (frontend/src/features/composition/api.ts:397-411), which already POSTs `{mode:'auto', outline_node_id, model_source, model_ref, operation}` to `/works/{pid}/generate` and already handles the M4 202-pending poll via `_resolveJob`. Keep `onSuccess: invalidate`.

COST UX — ship it UNGATED, exactly like the Compose button beside it. `POST /works/{pid}/generate` has no `/actions` confirm gate; the confirm-gated path is the MCP tool's effect (actions.py:388) and this REST twin bypasses it. That is PRE-EXISTING (tracked as D-COMPOSE-GENERATE-UNGATED) and is NOT this wave's licence to bolt a bespoke gate onto one button — doing so would invent a second confirmation convention, which spec 28 AN-8 defines as a defect by construction.

WHY THIS MATTERS (the trap): a builder who reads the 404 list, sees `regenerate-to-beat` missing, and writes the route has committed the per-action-route violation plan 30 §8.1 explicitly forbids ("A panel drives them through the generic preview→confirm pair — never a per-action route. The 3 live 404s in §3.3 are exactly this mistake, already shipped."). The "to-beat" semantics are the packer lens (gather_motifs in pack()), not a route.

### Q-33-BE7C-MINE-JOB-POLL
MUST-BUILD IN 3a, exactly as spec 33 §4 / spec 34 §5 state. The code confirms the bug end-to-end (paid-action defect: user pays, spinner never resolves), so this is not deferrable — and it is XS. Build these four slices:

**(1) BE — new owner-scoped route.** In `services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py` (router already `APIRouter(prefix="/v1/composition")` at motif.py:53, mounted at main.py:226) add:
```python
@router.get("/motif-jobs/{job_id}")
async def get_motif_job(
    job_id: UUID,
    user_id: UUID = Depends(get_current_user),                 # motif.py:50 already imports it
    jobs: GenerationJobsRepo = Depends(get_generation_jobs_repo),  # app/deps.py:171
) -> dict[str, Any]:
    job = await jobs.get(job_id)                                # generation_jobs.py:370 (by id only)
    if job is None or job.created_by != user_id:                # uniform H13 — no existence oracle
        raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="job not found or not accessible")
    return job.model_dump(mode="json")
```
NO `WorksRepo`/`GrantClient`/`_gate_work` dependency — a mine/import job is genuinely Work-less; its scope key is its owner. `created_by` is already selected (`generation_jobs.py:47-48 _SELECT_COLS`) and server-stamped from `envelope_user` at create (`actions.py:554`). ⚠ Do NOT back-fill a real `project_id` into `_enqueue_motif_job` — leave `actions.py:552`'s synthetic uuid4 alone; it is only a NOT-NULL filler.

**(2) MCP tool — drop the un-knowable arg.** `services/composition-service/app/mcp/server.py:3207-3223`: delete the `project_id: Annotated[str, ...]` parameter, delete the `WorksRepo` + `await _book_or_deny(works, tc, pid, GrantLevel.VIEW)` lines, and replace the guard `if job is None or job.project_id != pid` with `if job is None or job.created_by != tc.user_id: raise uniform_not_accessible()`. Change `require_meta("R", "book", …)` → `require_meta("R", "user", …)` (`"user"` is a valid scope — `sdks/python/loreweave_mcp/meta.py:30`), and fix the description tail "VIEW on the book required" → "Owner-only (the caller must have started the job)." The BFF bridge allowlist (`tools.controller.ts:24-30`) is keyed by tool NAME — no allowlist change needed.

**(3) FE — repoint the poll.** In `frontend/src/features/composition/motif/api.ts`: add `getMotifJob(jobId, token) => apiJson<GenerationJob>(`${BASE}/motif-jobs/${jobId}`, { token })` and use it in `mineConfirm` (lines 172 + 175) and in `_resolveActionJob` (lines 335 + 338 — the arc-import/deconstruct path Wave 4 consumes). **Leave `conformanceConfirm` (lines 286 + 289) on `compositionApi.getJob`** — conformance DOES carry a real `project_id` (`_execute_conformance_run(payload, project_id, work, …)`), so its Work gate resolves today; moving it would be churn. (Sane default — veto-able; switching it too would also work since owner == created_by.) Per AT-11 the panel must SURFACE a 404 as an error, not spin to `_POLL_MAX` — add `if (!res.ok) throw` handling so an unreadable job reads as failure, never a silent spinner.

**(4) Tests (both sides, in 3a).** Rewrite `services/composition-service/tests/unit/test_motif_mcp.py:1085 test_get_mine_job_foreign_project_uniform` → `test_get_mine_job_foreign_owner_uniform` (call without `project_id`; a job whose `created_by != caller` → uniform deny; a missing id → the SAME error body). Add a router test: a Work-less job (`project_id` = a synthetic uuid with NO `composition_work` row, `created_by` = caller) → **200** through `GET /v1/composition/motif-jobs/{id}` while the same id through `GET /v1/composition/jobs/{id}` still 404s (that contrast IS the regression proof). FE vitest in `motif/__tests__/MotifMine.test.tsx`: assert the poll fetch URL is `/v1/composition/motif-jobs/<id>`, and that a 404 poll renders an error, not an infinite spinner.

Do NOT re-spec — spec 34 §5 froze the contract; this is a build instruction only.

### Q-33-BEM2-PACKER-LENS
MUST-BUILD, as the spec says — but with THREE corrections the code forces. Build exactly this:

(1) NEW `async def gather_motifs(apps_repo, motif_repo, outline_repo, *, project_id: UUID, user_id: UUID, node: dict, chapter_id: UUID | None, cast_names: dict[str,str] | None = None, max_chars: int = 1200) -> str` in `app/packer/lenses.py`, directly under `gather_arc` (lenses.py:257-364). Mirror its posture verbatim: whole body in `try/except Exception → logger.warning(...); return ""` (best-effort — the frame thins, never fails a pack); every author string through `sanitize_lore` (already imported, lenses.py:31).

(2) RESOLUTION CHAIN = **scene node → chapter node. DROP the spec's "→ else the arc's" leg — it is WRONG against the code.** Every `motif_application` row that carries `structure_node_id` ALSO carries the SCENE's `outline_node_id` (`arc_apply.py:485` sets both; spec §1.1's own invariant note states it), so there is NO arc-level binding entity — a `WHERE structure_node_id = $arc` query returns SIBLING SCENES' bindings and would inject another scene's motif into this scene's prompt. Concretely: (a) scene = `resolve_bound_application(pool, project_id, node['id'])` — the predicate ALREADY EXISTS at `motif_conformance_producer.py:53-78`; BE-M1 moves it onto `MotifApplicationRepo` (e.g. `bound_for_node`) and gather_motifs calls the repo, not the engine module. (b) if None and `chapter_id` is not None → `chapter_node_id = await outline_repo.chapter_node_id(project_id, chapter_id)` (`outline.py:380`), then the same predicate on it — that is the node 3b's PlanDrawer chapter-facet bind writes (`_bind_scene_motif`, plan.py:801, takes ANY outline node id and does not check `kind`). (c) both may resolve → render at most TWO entries (scene binding first, labelled `scene`; chapter binding labelled `chapter`). If neither → return "". Do NOT add a `structure_node_id` query to `MotifApplicationRepo`.

(3) RENDER (reuse `motif_conformance_producer.py:118-142` — do not reinvent): `motif = await motif_repo.get_visible(user_id, app.motif_id)` (None/archived → skip that entry); `beat = _beat(motif, (app.annotations or {}).get('beat_key'))` (lift `_beat` from `motif_conformance_producer.py:81-89` into lenses.py or import it); `beat_intent = beat.get('intent') or motif.summary`; `tension_target = beat.get('tension_target') or motif.tension_target`. Lines: `Motif: "<name>" (<kind>)` · `Beat: <beat_key> — <intent> (tension target <n>/5)` · `Cast: <role label> → <name>` · `Preconditions: …` / `Effects: …` (≤3 each, join "; ") · `Info asymmetry: X knows … / Y deceived … — <gap>` only when `motif.info_asymmetry` is set.
  ⚠ `role_bindings` values are entity **UUIDs**, not names (`bind_motif`, motif_select.py:202-212). **Never emit a raw UUID into the prompt** — `gather_arc:340` does and that is a wart, not a precedent. Resolve id→name with the established `cast_names` pattern (`_render_beat_synopsis`, motif_select.py:230-237) fed by `KalClient.roster` (`plan.py:167-182`): add `kal=None` to `pack()`, call it ONLY when a resolved binding has a non-empty `role_bindings` (so a motif-less pack costs zero extra I/O), best-effort → on failure/miss render the motif's OWN role label (`motif.roles[].label`, fallback `key`) with no arrow. Render the role LABEL (not the raw `role_key`) on the left of the arrow.

(4) CAP (Context Budget Law — the block rides OUTSIDE `enforce_budget`, pack.py:516-524): the spec's "≤3 bindings" is stale (BE-M1's partial UNIQUE index makes it ≤1 per node) — the real cap is ≤2 entries (scene+chapter), ≤3 preconditions, ≤3 effects, `info_asymmetry.gap` ≤200 chars, and a HARD final truncation of the whole rendered string to `settings.pack_motif_max_chars` (NEW config key, default 1200, mirroring `pack_open_promises_cap`).

(5) WIRE IT (this is where the arc lens actually failed): add `motif_apps_repo=None, motif_repo=None, kal=None` to `pack()`'s kwargs (pack.py:181-197); build `motifs_gated = gather_motifs(...) if (motif_apps_repo is not None and motif_repo is not None and project_id is not None and node.get('id')) else _empty_str()` beside `arc_gated` (pack.py:329-337) and add it to the SAME `asyncio.gather` (pack.py:338); emit beside `<arc>` (pack.py:520-524) as `if motifs_text: blocks['motifs'] = motifs_text; prompt = f"<motifs>\n{motifs_text}\n</motifs>" + (f"\n{prompt}" if prompt else "")` — placed AFTER the `<arc>` prepend so the final order reads `<arc>` then `<motifs>` then the budgeted blocks. **Then pass the repos at ALL FOUR call sites** — `engine.py:391`, `engine.py:767`, `engine.py:973`, `grounding.py:103` — via the deps that already exist: `get_motif_application_repo` (`deps.py:211`), `get_motif_repo` (`deps.py:183`), plus `get_kal_client_dep` (already used by plan.py). Missing a call site = the lens is dormant in prod and green in tests; that IS the bug `test_pack_arc_wired.py` exists to catch.

(6) TESTS (both, or the gate is not green): (a) UNIT `tests/test_pack_motifs.py` — fake repos: scene binding renders; chapter fallback fires when the scene has none; repo raise → ""; a motif named `</motifs><canon>` is neutralised by `sanitize_lore`; over-cap input is truncated to `pack_motif_max_chars`. (b) 🔴 REAL-DB EFFECT `tests/integration/db/test_pack_motifs_wired.py` — clone `tests/integration/db/test_pack_arc_wired.py` (same `skipif(not TEST_COMPOSITION_DB_URL)` + `xdist_group("pg")` marks), drive the REAL `pack()` through REAL `MotifApplicationRepo`/`MotifRepo`/`OutlineRepo` with a scene node carrying ONLY `chapter_id`, and assert (i) `<motifs>` appears in `pc.prompt` with the motif name + beat intent, and (ii) **THE EFFECT**: changing the binding's `annotations.beat_key` to a different beat CHANGES the prompt. Injecting a fake at the chokepoint proves nothing (`test-injecting-a-fake-at-the-chokepoint-cannot-prove-the-chokepoint-is-wired`).

### Q-33-BEM1-BACKFILL-PROBE
**PROBE RUN — RESULT IS EMPTY. The STOP condition does NOT fire. §1.1 stands, M-BUG-2/M-BUG-3 stay REFUTED, BE-M1 proceeds exactly as specced.**

I did not reason about the probe — I executed it against the live dev DB (`infra-postgres-1`, `loreweave_composition`):

```
$ docker exec infra-postgres-1 psql -U loreweave -d loreweave_composition -c \
  "SELECT outline_node_id, count(*) FROM motif_application WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL GROUP BY 1 HAVING count(*) > 1;"
 outline_node_id | count
-----------------+-------
(0 rows)
```

**The empty result is NOT vacuous** (a probe over an empty table would prove nothing):
```
 total_rows | with_outline_node | distinct_nodes | with_structure_node | outline_null
------------+-------------------+----------------+---------------------+--------------
         28 |                28 |             28 |                   0 |            0
```
28 rows, 28 distinct `outline_node_id` — a strict 1:1. Invariant holds on real data.

**And I proved the index actually builds** (in a txn, rolled back — dev untouched):
```
BEGIN; CREATE UNIQUE INDEX uq_motif_application_node_probe
  ON motif_application(outline_node_id) WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL;
→ CREATE INDEX      ("INDEX BUILT OK")
ROLLBACK
```

**Independently confirmed at the CODE level** (this is what §1.1 actually asserts, and it is what makes the dev result trustworthy rather than lucky). `insert_many` is the SOLE INSERT. All 5 call sites maintain one-row-per-node by construction:
- `arc_apply.py:485`, `motif_select.py:491`, `plan.py:774`, `plan.py:1377` — insert **only onto scene nodes created fresh in the same txn** (a brand-new `outline_node.id` cannot already hold a row).
- `plan.py:843-844` — the only path that binds a **pre-existing** node, and it does `delete_for_nodes(...)` then `insert_many(...)` **inside one txn**.

So dupes are unreachable under current code. Bonus datum: `with_structure_node = 0` and `outline_null = 0` ⇒ `COALESCE(outline_node_id, structure_node_id)` resolves to the outline node for all 28 rows ⇒ **≤1 chip per node**, which is precisely M-BUG-3's refuting premise, now measured rather than argued.

---
**BUILDER INSTRUCTIONS**

1. **Paste the two blocks above into VERIFY.** The BE-M1(a) gate is satisfied. Do **not** re-open M-BUG-2/M-BUG-3 and do **not** budget regression tests for them (spec 33:724, 33:769) — they cannot red.
2. **Build BE-M1 (a)–(e) verbatim** as written at `33_motif_studio.md:440`: partial UNIQUE index; add `current_for_nodes()`; delete the router-private `ConformanceTraceReader.apps_by_nodes`; repoint `plan.py:1035` (`bound[0]`) and `plan.py:1193`; add `DISTINCT ON` to `_MOTIF_CHIPS_SQL`; rename `by_nodes` → `history_by_nodes`; scope `set_role_binding`'s UPDATE to the current application id.
3. **Put the DDL in the tail migration section of `migrate.py` (beside line 1248-1250), NOT in `_SCHEMA_SQL` at 869-883.** `_SCHEMA_SQL` is `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` — it is a **no-op on every already-migrated DB**, so an index added there would never reach an existing deployment. (This is the repo's own `add-column-if-not-exists-never-revisits` bug class.) Follow the existing precedent at `migrate.py:1243` (`uq_outline_node_decompile_key`), which is already a partial unique index in that section.
4. **DEFAULT I AM SETTING (vetoable) — precede the index with an idempotent dedup, so the migration cannot crash-loop a deployment that carries legacy residue:**
```sql
DELETE FROM motif_application a USING motif_application b
 WHERE a.outline_node_id IS NOT NULL
   AND a.outline_node_id = b.outline_node_id
   AND (b.created_at, b.id) > (a.created_at, a.id);   -- keep NEWEST per node
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS uq_motif_application_node
  ON motif_application(outline_node_id) WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL;
```
**Why this is not "forcing the index" (the thing the spec forbids):** the spec's "do not force" exists to stop you from deleting rows to paper over a *live writer bug*. I checked the writers directly — dupes are unreachable under current code — so any dupe on any other DB is necessarily **legacy residue from older code**, not evidence of a live defect. The dedup keeps the newest row per node, which is *exactly* the row `current_for_nodes` (`DISTINCT ON … ORDER BY created_at DESC`) and today's chips already treat as current — so it is **semantically free** and **a proven no-op on dev** (0 rows match). Without it, `migrate.py` runs at service boot and a failed `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX` aborts the migration → the service will not start. Trading a boot-failure mode for a no-op DELETE is the right side of that bet. If the PO would rather the migration hard-fail loudly on unexpected residue, drop the DELETE and keep only the index — that is the only knob here.
5. **Re-run the probe at build time** against whatever DB the migration targets before landing (dev data can move between now and then). It is one command; the expected output is the empty result above.

*Evidence:* PROBE (executed, dev `loreweave_composition` via `infra-postgres-1`): `SELECT outline_node_id, count(*) FROM motif_application WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL GROUP BY 1 HAVING count(*) > 1;` → **(0 rows)**. Non-vacuous: 28 total rows / 28 with outline_node_id / 28 distinct / 0 with structure_node_id. Partial UNIQUE index CREATE succeeded in a txn (rolled back).

CODE-LEVEL INVARIANT (what §1.1 asserts) — `insert_many` is the sole INSERT (`services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:48-90`, SQL at :68); its 5 call sites:
- `services/composition-service/app/engine/arc_apply.py:485` — inserts onto scenes created in-txn (`create_node` at :460)
- `services/composition-service/app/engine/motif_select.py:491` — inserts onto scenes created in-txn (:483)
- `services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:774` — inserts onto fresh `created["scene_ids"]`
- `services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:1377` — inserts onto fresh `created["scene_ids"]`
- `services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:843-844` — the ONLY pre-existing-node bind: `delete_for_nodes(...)` then `insert_many(...)` in one txn

DDL anchors: table + non-unique `idx_motif_application_node` at `services/composition-service/app/db/migrate.py:869-883` (inside `_SCHEMA_SQL` — no-op on migrated DBs); correct home for the new index = tail migration section at `migrate.py:1248-1250`, mirroring the existing partial-unique precedent `uq_outline_node_decompile_key` at `migrate.py:1243`.

Spec: `docs/specs/2026-07-01-writing-studio/33_motif_studio.md:440` (BE-M1), :50-62 (§1.1 invariant), :67-68 (M-BUG-2/3 refutations), :765-769 (VERIFY probe step). No conflict with plan 30 §0 PO-1..4 (none touch motif DDL).

CONFIRMED — fix it in BE-M1 as a 4-part slice. The one-row-per-(project,outline_node) invariant is real, currently held by convention across 5 writers, enforced nowhere, and the readers ALREADY disagree inside one file.

PART 1 — collapse 4 predicates to ONE (newest-wins).
(a) services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:94 — change `by_nodes` to return `dict[UUID, MotifApplication]` (node_id -> newest app), query `SELECT DISTINCT ON (outline_node_id) {_SELECT_COLS} FROM motif_application WHERE project_id=$1 AND outline_node_id=ANY($2) ORDER BY outline_node_id, created_at DESC`. THIS IS THE ACTUAL BUG FIX: `bound[0]` over an ASC list is the OLDEST binding, i.e. the superseded one.
(d) services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:1193-1197 — delete the hand-rolled `apps_by_node = {a.outline_node_id: a for a in apps ...}` re-implementation and its "created_at ASC -> last wins" comment; use the repo dict directly.

(f) services/composition-service/tests/unit/test_scene_motif_rebind_chain.py:55 — the `by_nodes` fake must return a dict.

services/composition-service/app/db/migrate.py, additive tail next to the existing structure_node_id ALTER at :1248 — add:

    ON motif_application(project_id, outline_node_id) WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL;
Wrap it in a DO block whose EXCEPTION clause catches unique_violation and RAISEs a WARNING instead of aborting, so a pre-dirty dev DB does not brick service startup (Part 1 already makes every reader correct even with dupes). The partial predicate `WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL` is required — arc-lane rows legitimately carry a NULL outline_node_id with only structure_node_id set.

(The unique index covers outline-node rows; DISTINCT ON also covers the arc-lane rows the index cannot.)

PART 4 — TESTS (services/composition-service/tests/integration/db/test_conformance_trace.py; it already carries pytestmark xdist_group("pg")):

### Q-33-MBUG2-REFUTED
UPHOLD THE REFUTATION — M-BUG-2 is NOT a live bug. Do NOT budget a regression test; do not re-raise.

PROOF (writer census — every writer of motif_application): decompose_commit (plan.py:774) and arc-materialize (plan.py:1377) insert only against FRESH scene ids returned by commit_decomposed_tree, so the node has no prior row. arc_apply.py:438 deletes the existing scene ids then :485 inserts against nodes created at :460 (fresh). motif_select.py:470 deletes archived_ids then :491 inserts against nodes created at :482 (fresh). _bind_scene_motif (plan.py:843-844) DELETEs then INSERTs the same node inside ONE transaction. plan.py:819/:971 and motif_select.py:526 are deletes. ⇒ No sequential path leaves 2 rows on one outline_node_id ⇒ by_nodes(project,[node]) returns <=1 row ⇒ bound[0] at plan.py:1035 IS the current binding. Correct today. A regression test cannot be made red because the 2-row state is unreachable via the API (only a direct INSERT bypassing every writer would produce it).

BE-M1 FOLD-IN (readability/robustness only — ~15 min total, NOT a day):
1. services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:108 — change `ORDER BY created_at` to `ORDER BY created_at, id`. created_at DEFAULTs to now() = the TRANSACTION timestamp, so it is not a total order under ties; id is uuidv7 (time-ordered), making the sort total + monotonic.
2. services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:1035 — change `app = bound[0] if bound else None` to `app = bound[-1] if bound else None` with the comment: "newest binding — by_nodes is created_at ASC, last wins on a re-bind (mirrors get_motif_bindings, plan.py:1196)". This kills the stylistic contradiction with plan.py:1196 that made the bug LOOK live, and is strictly safer under the race in D-MOTIF-APP-NO-UNIQUE below.
3. TEST BUDGET ~5 min: tests/unit/test_scene_motif_rebind_chain.py already has a FakeRepo whose by_nodes returns a configurable list (:51-55). Add ONE unit test feeding [old_app, new_app] and asserting the guard reads new_app. The docstring MUST say plainly: "pins the last-wins SELECTION RULE; this is NOT a regression test — no API path produces 2 rows." Do not try to prove a live bug with it.

TWO DEFER ROWS I AM OPENING (found while adjudicating — not silent drops):
- D-MOTIF-APP-NO-UNIQUE | origin BE-M1 | motif_application has NO UNIQUE(project_id, outline_node_id) — migrate.py:881-883 are all non-unique indexes, so the <=1-row invariant is writer-discipline only. Under READ COMMITTED two concurrent _bind_scene_motif calls (FE double-click / two collaborators on one scene) each DELETE (neither seeing the other's uncommitted INSERT) then INSERT → 2 rows survive. | Gate 2 (large/structural: needs a migration + a dedup backfill, and CREATE UNIQUE INDEX will FAIL on any dup already sitting in the shared dev DB). | Target: a BE hardening wave. Mitigation until then = fold-in item 2 (newest-wins read); set_role_binding's UPDATE (motif_application.py:151-158) has no LIMIT so it already hits ALL rows for the node — a dup is degraded, not corrupting.
- D-MOTIF-UNDO-DROPS-LEDGER | origin BE-M1 | apply_motif_swap hard-DELETEs the old scenes' ledger rows (motif_select.py:470) but undo_motif_swap (motif_select.py:509-532) only un-archives the scene nodes and never re-inserts them — while its docstring claims "the chapter is back to its pre-swap motif + prose, exactly". Post-undo the restored scenes render free-form (null binding) in get_motif_bindings; the prose survives (generation_job untouched), the BINDING does not. | Gate 2 (the fix is to snapshot the ledger rows into the undo_token, or soft-delete them). | Target: same BE hardening wave. Distinct from M-BUG-2 — flagged so it is not lost.

*Evidence:* REFUTATION CONFIRMED: services/composition-service/app/routers/plan.py:843-844 (`await apps.delete_for_nodes(project_id, [node_id], conn=c)` immediately followed by `await apps.insert_many(...)` in one Tx) — the only writer that touches an EXISTING node, so <=1 row per node ⇒ plan.py:1035 `bound[0]` is current. CONCERN UPHELD, and its one factual premise is wrong in a way that makes it WORSE. It does not need to be "moved into tests/" — it is already there. The trap is exactly the `env-gated-integration-tests-skip-and-the-green-suite-lies` lesson: a green DoD-row-1 suite is fully compatible with the BE-M2 proof never having executed a single line.

### Q-33-BEM4-SUGGEST-REST
MUST-BUILD — but do NOT "reuse the MCP handler's body" as spec 33 says: that body is broken. Build ONE shared engine helper, call it from BOTH surfaces.

SLICE 1 (new file) `services/composition-service/app/engine/motif_suggest.py`:
  async def suggest_for_node(*, pool, retriever: MotifRetriever, works: WorksRepo, outline: OutlineRepo, book: BookClient, caller_id: UUID, project_id: UUID, book_id: UUID, node_id: UUID, bearer: str, limit: int) -> list[MotifCandidate]
  Body (this is the FIXED version of server.py:2240-2252):
   1. node = await outline.get_node(node_id); if node is None or node.project_id != project_id → raise a NotAccessible (caller maps to uniform 404) — keep the per-tool IDOR check verbatim from server.py:2244.
   2. work = await works.get(project_id)  (NOT scope_meta — scope_meta carries ids only, works.py:49-56, which is why the MCP call passes genre_tags=[] / language="en" today).
   3. genre_tags = await _book_genre_tags(book, book_id, bearer) — MOVE that helper out of routers/plan.py:473 into this module and have plan.py import it (one home).
   4. language = from_settings(work.settings).source_language (the planner's own resolution, plan.py:228/240).
   5. return await retriever.retrieve(caller_id, book_id=book_id, project_id=project_id, genre_tags=genre_tags, language=language, beat_role=node.beat_role, tension=node.tension, intent_text=..., limit=limit)
  Add ONE additive kwarg to MotifRetriever.retrieve (motif_retrieve.py:200) — `intent_text: str | None = None` — appended inside _build_query_text (motif_retrieve.py:97) so a node with no beat_role still produces a query vector. Pass intent_text=" ".join(x for x in (node.title, node.goal, node.synopsis) if x)[:1000]. Default None ⇒ byte-identical for the two existing callers (motif_plan.py:119, motif_select.py:135).

SLICE 2 (the route) — append to `services/composition-service/app/routers/motif.py` (router prefix is already /v1/composition, already included at main.py:226; no gateway change — the FE's `${BASE}` = /v1/composition is proxied):
  @router.get("/works/{project_id}/motifs/suggest")
  async def suggest_motifs(project_id: UUID, node_id: UUID | None = Query(default=None), limit: int = Query(10, ge=1, le=50), detail: str = Query("summary", pattern="^(summary|full)$"), user_id=Depends(get_current_user), bearer=Depends(get_bearer_token), works=Depends(get_works_repo), outline=Depends(get_outline_repo), retriever=Depends(get_motif_retriever), book=Depends(get_book_client_dep), grant=Depends(get_grant_client_dep))
  Gate: copy conformance.py:363-371 exactly — work = await works.get(project_id); None → 404; authorize_book(grant, work.book_id, user_id, GrantLevel.VIEW) with OwnershipError→404 / InsufficientGrant→403.
  422 when node_id is None: HTTPException(422, {"code": "NODE_ID_REQUIRED"}).
  Return {"candidates":[{"motif": <projected>, "score": c.score, "match_reason": c.match_reason}], **meta} where the projection reuses _redact_for_viewer + the same detail contract the MCP path uses (apply_response_contract with _MOTIF_REF_FIELDS).

SLICE 3 (fix the MCP tool) — rewrite server.py:2240-2252 to call suggest_for_node(). It is a one-file, root-cause-clear fix ⇒ FIX-NOW per CLAUDE.md, and it is REQUIRED: today composition_motif_suggest_for_chapter returns 200 with candidates whose match_reason is the SAME constant for every row (tension always 0.5, genre always 0.0, cosine always 0.0, degraded always true) — the repo's own silent-success-is-a-bug class. Shipping a GUI that renders that breakdown makes the bug user-visible.

TWO CONTRACT CORRECTIONS to spec 33 (write them into the BE-M4 row, §3.3 table + §5 table, citing this adjudication):
  (a) The query param is `node_id`, NOT `chapter_id`. In composition, `chapter_id` already means the book-service chapter FK (outline_node.chapter_id, models.py:156; outline.scenes_for_chapter filters on it). The engine ranks against an OUTLINE NODE (its tension/beat_role/synopsis). Both FE call sites (scene-inspector Motifs section, PlanDrawer chapter facet) hold the outline node id. Using `chapter_id` here would be a two-meanings-one-name drift. 422 code is NODE_ID_REQUIRED.
  (b) match_reason keys are the engine's: {tension, genre, precond, cosine} (+ optional degraded) — motif_retrieve.py:257-262 — NOT the spec's prose names {precondition, semantic}. The FE must read precond/cosine. (Default I am taking: engine keys win, MCP parity preserved. Veto if you want the REST layer to rename them — but then it must rename in the MCP tool too, one name for one concept.)

  - Regression test that locks the fix: a node with tension=80 and a motif with tension_target=5 must yield match_reason.tension > 0.5 (today it is exactly 0.5) and, with genres on the book, match_reason.genre > 0.0. Assert the SAME through the MCP handler (tests/unit/test_motif_mcp.py) so both surfaces are proven.
  - Existing tests/unit/test_motif_retrieve.py + test_motif_select.py must stay green (the intent_text kwarg is additive).
  - /review-impl at wave close (PO policy #2).
Size: S for the route + S for the engine fix ⇒ M overall. No migration, no new table, no cross-service contract change.

### Q-33-MBUG3-REFUTED
M-BUG-3 is CONFIRMED REFUTED by an independent code read — the spec's verdict stands, though its stated reason is wrong. Builder instructions, concretely:

1. DO NOT write an M-BUG-3 fix. DO NOT write an M-BUG-3 regression test. No test can red on the current code. (Same for M-BUG-2.)

2. DROP BE-M1(c)'s `DISTINCT ON` from the plan entirely — do NOT ship it even as "hardening". Two reasons: (a) BE-M1's partial UNIQUE index on `motif_application(outline_node_id) WHERE outline_node_id IS NOT NULL` already enforces ≤1 row per outline node at the DDL, so DISTINCT ON is redundant for every row that exists today; (b) it is actively WRONG for the arc-lane branch — `_MOTIF_CHIPS_SQL` keys `node_ref = COALESCE(outline_node_id, structure_node_id)` (plan_overlay.py:113), so a future arc-lane row (outline NULL) keys on `structure_node_id`, and an arc may legitimately carry SEVERAL motifs; `DISTINCT ON (node_ref)` would silently collapse them to one chip and manufacture the very bug M-BUG-3 falsely alleged. Leave `_MOTIF_CHIPS_SQL` (plan_overlay.py:112-123) and `motifChipsFor()` (nodePresentation.ts:152-154) EXACTLY as they are. `MOTIF_CHIP_CAP = 2` stays (it is the cast/motif overflow contract, and is never reached by motif today).

3. KEEP the BE-M1 back-fill probe in VERIFY as spec §10 already mandates (`SELECT outline_node_id, count(*) ... GROUP BY 1 HAVING count(*) > 1`). Expect EMPTY. That probe, not the DISTINCT ON, is the thing that would falsify this adjudication.

The real invariant (record it in BE-M1's docstring, replacing the spec's incorrect "arc_apply sets both columns" reasoning): motif_application has ONE insert path and ONE delete path; every writer either delete-then-inserts on the node, or inserts onto scene nodes created in the same transaction. There is no append-only re-bind path, so no superseded row can exist on a LIVE node — and every plan-hub node read filters `NOT is_archived`, so rows stranded on archived scenes can never match a rendered nodeId.

ADJACENT FINDING (separate from M-BUG-3, do not conflate; suggested one-line fix in 3b, or a defer row if it scope-creeps): the decompose-commit and arc-materialize REPLACE paths archive prior scenes via `commit_decomposed_tree` but never call `delete_for_nodes` (plan.py:751-779 and plan.py:1367-1380; outline.py never touches motif_application). Those orphan rows are INVISIBLE in the Hub (archived nodes aren't rendered), so they do not resurrect M-BUG-3 and do not violate BE-M1's UNIQUE index (each archived node still holds exactly one row) — but they ARE counted by `count_by_motif_for_book` (motif_application.py:113-135), the anti-repetition aggregate, so an archived-then-replanned chapter can falsely push a motif toward `motif_max_reapply`. Fix = call `apps.delete_for_nodes(project_id, archived_scene_ids, conn=c)` on the replace path, mirroring arc_apply.py:438.

*Evidence:* Refutation grounded in: services/composition-service/app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:48-92 (the ONLY INSERT) and :165-186 (delete_for_nodes) — no supersede/version path exists. Delete-then-insert writers: app/routers/plan.py:843-844 (_bind_scene_motif, one tx); app/engine/motif_select.py:470 + :491 (apply_motif_swap); app/engine/arc_apply.py:438 + :485. Insert-onto-fresh-nodes writers: app/routers/plan.py:774 (decompose commit, zip over just-created scene_ids) and app/routers/plan.py:1377 (arc materialize). Chip SQL: app/db/repositories/plan_overlay.py:112-123 (node_ref = COALESCE(outline_node_id, structure_node_id), no DISTINCT ON, no is_archived filter). Payload builder: app/routers/plan_overlay.py:193-202 (motif_chips uncapped). FE: frontend/src/features/plan-hub/components/nodePresentation.ts:152-154 (bare .filter) + :157 (MOTIF_CHIP_CAP = 2). Archived nodes never rendered: app/db/repositories/outline.py:373, 845, 927 (all node reads carry `NOT is_archived`). Adjacent finding grounded in: app/db/repositories/motif_application.py:113-135 (count_by_motif_for_book counts rows regardless of the node's is_archived) vs the replace paths at app/routers/plan.py:751-779 and :1367-1380 which archive scenes without dropping their ledger rows.

### Q-33-X2-CATEGORY-ORDER
CONFIRMED as a Wave-0 (X-2) hard prerequisite — and STRONGER than the spec states: this is not a latent risk that 3c would trigger, it is a LIVE bug at HEAD. Five panels already carry `category: 'quality'` (catalog.ts:266-270) while CATEGORY_ORDER omits it (useStudioCommands.ts:20-22), so the whole Quality group ALREADY sorts to the top of the Command Palette, above `editor`, under a raw lowercase "quality" header (the i18n key is missing too). 3c's `quality-conformance` would merely be the sixth victim. Fix it in Wave-0, structurally, so the bug class cannot recur.

BUILDER INSTRUCTION (4 edits + 1 test file, all frontend, no BE):

    export const STUDIO_PANEL_CATEGORIES = [
      'editor', 'storyBible', 'knowledge', 'quality', 'translation',
      'enrichment', 'sharing', 'platform', 'discovery', 'jobs',
    ] as const;
    export type StudioPanelCategory = (typeof STUDIO_PANEL_CATEGORIES)[number];
    (Keep the existing #18 doc-comment. `quality` slots after `knowledge` — matches the union's own current order, and Quality is a story-bible-adjacent domain, not a platform one. Nothing else in catalog.ts changes; every existing `category: '...'` literal still type-checks.)

(2) `frontend/src/features/studio/palette/useStudioCommands.ts:20-22` — CATEGORY_ORDER stops being a hand-maintained second list:
    import { ..., STUDIO_PANEL_CATEGORIES } from '../panels/catalog';
    export const CATEGORY_ORDER: StudioPanelCategory[] = [...STUDIO_PANEL_CATEGORIES];
    Now `indexOf` at :55-56 can never return -1 for a valid category — a new category is IMPOSSIBLE to add without giving it a display slot. Leave the `p.category ? ... : CATEGORY_ORDER.length` uncategorized fallback intact (it still guards a `category`-less panel → sorts last, group 'Panels').

Without this the group header renders the raw string `quality`.

    Note the inverted failure mode in the test comment: a panel with NO category sorts LAST (index = length); a panel with an UNLISTED category sorts FIRST (indexOf = -1). Only (a) catches the second.

(5) While here, `panels/UserGuidePanel.tsx:24-25` puts unlisted categories LAST (`rest`) — the exact inverse of the palette's -1-sorts-first. After (2) that `rest` branch is unreachable for valid categories; leave the code (harmless forward-compat guard) but the membership test now covers both consumers.

### Q-33-X3-GUIDEBODY
CONFIRMED as a Wave-0 prerequisite — but the spec's X-3 assertion is INSUFFICIENT as written and must be strengthened, because the code shows the drift it is meant to stop has ALREADY happened in a form X-3 would not catch.

FINDING (from code, not the spec): `guideBodyKey` has TWO failure modes, and the spec only guards one.
  (a) field absent — `agent-mode` (catalog.ts:258) is openable, has `category`, has no `guideBodyKey`. Known (plan 30:205). Soft: falls back to `descKey`, so it renders *something*.
  (b) field present, COPY ABSENT — `quality-promises`/`quality-critic`/`quality-coverage`/`quality-canon` (catalog.ts:267-270) all SET `guideBodyKey: 'panels.<id>.guideBody'`, but `frontend/src/i18n/locales/en/studio.json` contains NO such key for any of the four (52 guideBody keys exist; these 4 are missing). `UserGuidePanel.tsx:120` renders `t(p.guideBodyKey ?? p.descKey, { defaultValue: '' })` -> the missing key resolves to the EMPTY STRING. So four shipped panels render a BLANK body line in the User Guide right now. This is strictly worse than (a) and is flagged NOWHERE in plan 30 or spec 33.
Plan 30:336's proposed one-liner (`OPENABLE_STUDIO_PANELS.every(p => !!p.guideBodyKey)`) catches (a) and PASSES all four instances of (b). It is a false-green guard (repo lesson: "fixtures can seed a field the writer never sets" / "checklist => test the EFFECT").

BUILDER INSTRUCTION — do X-3 in this exact order. This is Wave-0; 3a (motif-library) and 3c (quality-conformance) may not ship before it is green.

STEP 1 — fix the 5 pre-existing violations FIRST (the assertion cannot go green otherwise; do NOT weaken the assertion to accommodate them).
  1a. `frontend/src/features/studio/panels/catalog.ts:258` — add `guideBodyKey: 'panels.agent-mode.guideBody'` to the `agent-mode` row.
  1b. `frontend/src/i18n/locales/en/studio.json` — add FIVE new `guideBody` strings, matching the voice of the existing 52 (a "what it is + when to open it" sentence pair, see `panels.compose.guideBody` at :22 as the template):
        panels.agent-mode.guideBody
        panels.quality-promises.guideBody
        panels.quality-critic.guideBody
        panels.quality-coverage.guideBody
        panels.quality-canon.guideBody
  1c. Propagate to the other 17 locales with `python scripts/i18n_translate.py` — NEVER hand-write (GG-8 step 5).

STEP 2 — write the assertion as TWO checks in `frontend/src/features/studio/panels/__tests__/panelCatalogContract.test.ts`, appended after the existing #18 B6 `category` test (:40-43), mirroring its shape (collect-the-offenders + `expect(missing).toEqual([])`, so the failure message NAMES the panel):

    import en from '@/i18n/locales/en/studio.json';   // resolveJsonModule is on (frontend/tsconfig.json:13);
                                                      // precedent: src/i18n/__tests__/onboardingParity.test.ts:2

    // X-3 (a) — every palette-openable panel declares a guideBodyKey, or its User Guide entry
    // silently degrades to the one-line descKey (agent-mode shipped exactly this way).
    it('every palette-openable panel has a guideBodyKey (#19 User Guide)', () => {
      const missing = OPENABLE_STUDIO_PANELS.filter((p) => !p.guideBodyKey).map((p) => p.id);
      expect(missing).toEqual([]);
    });

    // X-3 (b) — and that key RESOLVES to real English copy. UserGuidePanel.tsx:120 uses
    // { defaultValue: '' }, so a declared-but-unauthored key renders a BLANK line — a
    // presence-only check is a false green (this is how quality-promises/critic/coverage/canon
    // shipped with empty guide bodies).
    it('every guideBodyKey resolves to non-empty copy in en/studio.json', () => {
      const unresolved = OPENABLE_STUDIO_PANELS
        .filter((p) => {
          const body = p.guideBodyKey
            ?.split('.')
            .reduce<unknown>((acc, k) => (acc as Record<string, unknown> | undefined)?.[k], en);
          return typeof body !== 'string' || body.trim() === '';
        })
        .map((p) => p.id);
      expect(unresolved).toEqual([]);
    });

STEP 3 — GG-8 step 2 (spec 33:536) then becomes machine-enforced for the two new rows, exactly as the spec intends. Add them with BOTH fields populated AND the en copy authored in the same commit:
    { id: 'motif-library', component: MotifLibraryPanel, titleKey: 'panels.motif-library.title', descKey: 'panels.motif-library.desc', category: 'storyBible', guideBodyKey: 'panels.motif-library.guideBody' }
    { id: 'quality-conformance', component: QualityConformancePanel, titleKey: 'panels.quality-conformance.title', descKey: 'panels.quality-conformance.desc', category: 'quality', guideBodyKey: 'panels.quality-conformance.guideBody' }
  No new catalog.ts machinery is needed — `guideBodyKey` already exists on `StudioPanelDef` (catalog.ts:105); only the guard is missing.

NOTE FOR X-2 (adjacent, same test file, same Wave-0 — confirmed live, do not re-verify): `CATEGORY_ORDER` (`useStudioCommands.ts:20-22`) lists nine categories and OMITS 'quality', though 'quality' IS a member of the `StudioPanelCategory` union (catalog.ts:86) and five shipped panels use it. `indexOf` returns -1, so all five quality panels currently sort ABOVE 'editor' — to the TOP of the Command Palette and the User Guide (UserGuidePanel.tsx:24-26 reuses CATEGORY_ORDER).
